Introduced Version
SENATE BILL No. 80
_____
DIGEST OF INTRODUCED BILL
Citations Affected: Numerous citations throughout the Indiana Code.
Synopsis: Code publication. Addresses unresolved amend-repeal
conflicts created during the 2025 legislative session. Repeals and
relocates the following chapters for organization of defined terms by
alphabetical order and to provide for future expansion of those
chapters: (1) IC 8-23-1, the Indiana department of transportation law
definitions chapter, which is relocated to a new IC 8-23-1.1. (2)
IC 12-7-2, the human services law definitions chapter, which is
relocated to a new IC 12-7-2.1. (3) IC 31-9-2, the family law and
juvenile law definitions chapter, which is relocated to a new
IC 31-9-2.1. Makes conforming cross-reference updates. Makes no
substantive change to law. (The introduced version of this bill was
prepared by the code revision committee.)
Effective: July 1, 2026; July 1, 2027; January 1, 2028.
Freeman, Taylor G
December 8, 2025, read first time and referred to Committee on Judiciary.
2026 IN 80—LS 6159/DI 112

Introduced
Second Regular Session of the 124th General Assembly (2026)
PRINTING CODE. Amendments: Whenever an existing statute (or a section of the Indiana
Constitution) is being amended, the text of the existing provision will appear in this style type,
additions will appear in this style type, and deletions will appear in this style type.
Additions: Whenever a new statutory provision is being enacted (or a new constitutional
provision adopted), the text of the new provision will appear in this style type. Also, the
word NEW will appear in that style type in the introductory clause of each SECTION that adds
a new provision to the Indiana Code or the Indiana Constitution.
Conflict reconciliation: Text in a statute in this style type or this style type reconciles conflicts
between statutes enacted by the 2025 Regular Session of the General Assembly.

A BILL FOR AN ACT to amend the Indiana Code concerning
general provisions.

5 include de-escalation training. Inservice training must also include:
6 (1) training:
7 (A) in interacting with persons with mental illness, addictive
8 disorders, intellectual disabilities, autism, developmental
9 disabilities, and Alzheimer's disease or related senile
10 dementia; and
11 (B) provided by persons approved by the secretary of family
12 and social services and the board;
13 (2) after December 31, 2024, annual training, which may be
14 completed online or by other means of virtual instruction, that
15 addresses the mental health and wellness of law enforcement
16 officers including:
17 (A) healthy coping skills to preserve the mental health of law
18 enforcement officers and manage the stress and trauma of
19 policing;
20 (B) recognizing:
21 (i) symptoms of posttraumatic stress disorder; and
22 (ii) signs of suicidal behavior; and
23 (C) information on mental health resources available for law
24 enforcement officers; and
25 (3) training concerning:
26 (A) human and sexual trafficking; and
27 (B) high risk missing persons (as defined in IC 5-2-17-1).
28 The board may approve courses offered by other public or private
29 training entities, including postsecondary educational institutions, as

6 SECTION 17. IC 5-2-17-1, AS AMENDED BY P.L.40-2024,
7 SECTION 1, IS AMENDED TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
8 JULY 1, 2026]: Sec. 1. As used in this chapter, "high risk missing
9 person" means a person whose whereabouts are not known and who
10 may be at risk of injury or death. The term includes the following:
11 (1) A person who is missing as the result of abduction by a
12 stranger.
13 (2) A person whose disappearance may be the result of the
14 commission of a crime.
15 (3) A person whose disappearance occurred under circumstances
16 that are inherently dangerous.
17 (4) A person who is missing for more than thirty (30) days.
18 (5) A missing person who is in need of medical attention or
19 prescription medication.
20 (6) A missing person who may be at risk due to abduction by a
21 noncustodial parent.
22 (7) A missing person who is mentally impaired.
23 (8) A missing person who is less than twenty-one (21) years of
24 age.
25 (9) A missing person who has previously been the victim of a
26 threat of violence or an act of violence.
27 (10) A missing person who has been determined by a law
28 enforcement agency to be:
29 (A) at risk of injury or death; or
30 (B) a person that meets any of the descriptions in subdivisions
31 (1) through (9).
32 (11) A missing person who is an endangered adult (as defined in
33 IC 12-7-2-131.3). IC 12-7-2.1-227).
34 (12) A missing person who is a veteran at risk (as defined in
35 IC 12-7-2-197.3). IC 12-7-2.1-346).

30 a whole and for which responsibility is assigned to the department.
31 Sec. 40. "Substantial completion" refers to the date, as
32 determined by the department, when the construction of the
33 contract is sufficiently completed in accordance with the plans and
34 specifications, as modified by any change orders, so that the
35 construction can be used for its intended purpose.
36 Sec. 41. "Transportation plan" means a statement evaluating

38 comprehensive actions to accomplish policy objectives.
39 Sec. 42. "Traveled way" means the part of the roadway for the
40 movement of vehicles. The term does not include shoulders or
41 auxiliary lanes.
42 Sec. 43. "Trimovement sign" means a sign that displays three

1 (3) separate images sequentially by rotating triangular cylinders.

20 (3) Personally visit each sex or violent offender in the county at
21 the sex or violent offender's listed address at least one (1) time per
22 year, beginning seven (7) days after the local law enforcement
23 authority receives a notice under section 7 of this chapter or the
24 date the sex or violent offender is:
25 (A) released from a penal facility (as defined in
26 IC 35-31.5-2-232), a secure private facility (as defined in
27 IC 31-9-2-115), IC 31-9-2.1-223), or a juvenile detention
28 facility;
29 (B) placed in a community transition program;
30 (C) placed in a community corrections program;
31 (D) placed on parole; or
32 (E) placed on probation;
33 whichever occurs first.
34 (4) Personally visit each sex or violent offender who is designated
35 a sexually violent predator under IC 35-38-1-7.5 at least once
36 every ninety (90) days, beginning seven (7) days after the local
37 law enforcement authority receives a notice under section 7 of
38 this chapter or the date the sex or violent offender is:
39 (A) released from a penal facility (as defined in
40 IC 35-31.5-2-232), a secure private facility (as defined in
41 IC 31-9-2-115), IC 31-9-2.1-223), or a juvenile detention
42 facility;
2026 IN 80—LS 6159/DI 112

62
1 (B) placed in a community transition program;
2 (C) placed in a community corrections program;
3 (D) placed on parole; or
4 (E) placed on probation;
5 whichever occurs first.
6 (b) If a sex or violent offender appears not to reside at the sex or
7 violent offender's listed address, the local law enforcement authority
8 shall immediately notify the department and the prosecuting attorney.

28 Medicaid services provided by facilities described in subsection (a).
29 (d) If federal financial participation to match the assessments in
30 subsection (a) becomes unavailable under federal law, the authority to
31 impose the assessments terminates on the date that the federal
32 statutory, regulatory, or interpretive change takes effect.

34 Sec. 92. (a) "Exigent circumstances", as applied to an action by
35 the department with regard to a child, means that:

204
1 the child's physical safety is seriously endangered;
2 (2) there is no less intrusive alternative to the department's
3 action that would reasonably and sufficiently protect the
4 child's imminent health or safety; and
5 (3) one (1) or more of the following applies:
6 (A) The parent, guardian, or custodian of the child:
7 (i) is the alleged perpetrator of the abuse or neglect of
8 the child; or
9 (ii) is allegedly aware of the abuse or neglect of the child
10 and has allegedly not ensured the child's safety.
11 (B) There is reason to believe that:
12 (i) the safety of the child might be jeopardized; or
13 (ii) essential evidence regarding signs or symptoms of
14 abuse or neglect under subdivision (1) on or in the child's
15 body might not be available;
16 if the department's action is delayed or the child's parent,
17 guardian, or custodian is notified before the department's
18 action.
19 (C) The child is a homeless unaccompanied minor and is
20 voluntarily receiving services at an emergency shelter or
21 shelter care facility without the presence or consent of the
22 child's parent, guardian, or custodian.
23 (b) An allegation of educational neglect does not qualify as an
24 exigent circumstance.

24 IC 31-9-2-22.5(4). IC 31-9-2.1-58(4).
25 (3) The individual's employment before the completion of the
26 criminal history check required under subsection (h) is limited to
27 training during which the individual:
28 (A) does not have contact with children who are under the care
29 and control of the group home; and
30 (B) does not have access to records containing information
31 regarding children who are under the care and control of the
32 group home.

1 date of the attestation.

29 (2) placement under this section is undetermined at the time the
30 predispositional report is prepared.
31 (d) The juvenile court may enter a dispositional decree approving
32 placement of a child in another home under section 1(a)(3) or
33 6(b)(2)(D) of this chapter or awarding wardship to a person or facility
34 that results in a placement with a person under section 1(a)(4) or
35 6(b)(2)(E) of this chapter if:
36 (1) a person described in subsection (a) has:
37 (A) committed an act resulting in a substantiated report of
38 child abuse or neglect;
39 (B) been convicted of:
40 (i) a felony under IC 9-30-5;
41 (ii) battery (IC 35-42-2-1);
42 (iii) criminal recklessness (IC 35-42-2-2) as a felony;
2026 IN 80—LS 6159/DI 112

289
1 (iv) criminal confinement (IC 35-42-3-3) as a felony;
2 (v) arson (IC 35-43-1-1) as a felony;
3 (vi) nonsupport of a dependent child (IC 35-46-1-5);
4 (vii) operating a motorboat while intoxicated (IC 35-46-9-6)
5 as a felony;
6 (viii) a felony involving a weapon under IC 35-47; or
7 (ix) a felony relating to controlled substances under
8 IC 35-48-4;
9 if the conviction did not occur within the past five (5) years; or
10 (C) had a juvenile adjudication for a nonwaivable offense, as
11 defined in IC 31-9-2-84.8 IC 31-9-2.1-168 that, if committed
12 by an adult, would be a felony; and
13 (2) the person's commission of the offense, delinquent act, or act
14 of abuse or neglect described in subdivision (1) is not relevant to
15 the person's present ability to care for a child, and placing the
16 child in another home is in the best interest of the child.
17 However, a court may not enter a dispositional decree placing a child

14 SECTION 251. IC 36-8-8-19, AS AMENDED BY P.L.6-2012,
15 SECTION 253, IS AMENDED TO READ AS FOLLOWS
16 [EFFECTIVE JULY 1, 2026]: Sec. 19. (a) The baseline statewide
17 physical examination required by section 7(a) of this chapter shall be
18 prescribed by the system board and shall be administered by the
19 appointing authority, as determined by the local board, after the
20 appointing authority extends a conditional offer for employment. The
21 baseline statewide physical examination shall be administered by a
22 licensed physician and must include all of the following:
23 (1) A general medical history.
24 (2) The tests identified in rules that shall be adopted by the system
25 board.
26 (b) The system board shall adopt minimum standards by rule that a
27 police officer or firefighter must meet for the baseline statewide
28 physical examination described in subsection (a). The baseline
29 statewide physical examination and related standards must:
30 (1) reflect the essential functions of the job;
31 (2) be consistent with business necessity; and
32 (3) be evaluated by the system board one (1) time before January
33 1, 2015, and every five (5) years thereafter.
34 (c) The system board shall, in consultation with the commissioner
35 of mental health, select the baseline statewide mental examination
36 described in section 7(a) of this chapter. The standards for passing the
37 baseline statewide mental examination shall be determined by the local
38 board. The baseline statewide mental examination and related
39 standards must:
40 (1) reflect the essential functions of the job;
41 (2) be consistent with business necessity; and
42 (3) be evaluated by the system board one (1) time before January

1 1, 2015, and every five (5) years thereafter.
